25:T2a65,<entryFree id="n21282" key="سَاقَ المَاشِيَةَ" type="main">     
                  <form>       
                     <itype>1</itype>        
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">سَاقَ المَاشِيَةَ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form>, (S, K,) or <foreign lang="ar">النَّعَمَ</foreign>, (Mgh,) or <foreign lang="ar">الدَّابَّةَ</foreign>, (Msb,) aor. <foreign lang="ar">يَسُوقُ</foreign>, (S, Mgh, Msb,) inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">سَوْقٌ</foreign> (S, Mgh, Msb, K) and <foreign lang="ar">سِيَاقٌ</foreign>, (S, [so in both of my copies, but it is said in the JK that this latter is used in relation to death, and such is generally the case,]) or <foreign lang="ar">سَيَاقٌ</foreign>, like <foreign lang="ar">سَحَابٌ</foreign>, (TA, [but this I have not found elsewhere, and I doubt its correctness,]) and <foreign lang="ar">سِيَاقَةٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">مَسَاقٌ</foreign>, (O, K, TA,) <hi rend="ital">He drove the cattle</hi> [or <hi rend="ital">the beast</hi>]; <hi rend="ital">he urged the cattle</hi> [or <hi rend="ital">the beast</hi>] <hi rend="ital">to go;</hi> (Mgh;) and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n21282-1" target="استاقها" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign> signifies the same, (S, K,) as also   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n21282-2" target="اساقها" n="2" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>, and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n21282-3" target="سوّقها" n="3" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n21282"/></foreign>; (TA;) or <foreign lang="ar">تَسْوِيقٌ</foreign>, the inf. n. [or this last], signifies the <hi rend="ital">driving well:</hi> (KL:) [and accord. to Freytag,   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n21282-4" target="استساق" n="4" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>, followed by an accus., signifies the same as <foreign lang="ar">سَاقَ</foreign> as expl. above; but for this he names no authority.] Hence, in the Kur [lxxv. 30], <foreign lang="ar">إِلَى رَبِّكَ يَوْمَئِذٍ المَسَاقُ</foreign> (TA) i. e. <hi rend="ital">To thy Lord,</hi> and his judgment, <hi rend="ital">on that day, shall be the driving.</hi> (Bd, Jel.) And the saying, in a trad., <foreign lang="ar">لَاتَقُومُ السَّاعَةُ حَتَّى يَخْرُجَ رَجُلٌ مِنْ قَحْطَانَ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">يَسُوقُ النَّاسَ بِعَصًاهُ</foreign> [properly rendered <hi rend="ital">The resurrection,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">the hour thereof, shall not come to pass until a man come forth from</hi> the tribe of <hi rend="ital">Kahtán driving the people with his staff</hi>], allusive to his having the mastery over them, and their obeying him; the staff being mentioned only to indicate his tyrannical and rough treatment of them. (TA.) [And hence the saying, <foreign lang="ar">ساق عَلَىَّ فُلَانًا</foreign> <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">He urged such a one to intercede for him with me.</hi>]          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  [Hence also,] <foreign lang="ar">سَاقَهُ القَدَرُ إِلَى مَا قُدِّرَ لَهُ</foreign> <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  [<hi rend="ital">Destiny drove him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">impelled him, to that which was destined for him</hi>]. (TA.) [And in like manner one says of desire, &amp;c.]          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  And <foreign lang="ar">ساق إِلَى</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">المَرْأَةِ مَهْرَهَا</foreign>, (K,) or <foreign lang="ar">صَدَاقَهَا</foreign>, (S, Msb,) inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">سِيَاقٌ</foreign>; (TA;) and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n21282-5" target="اساقهُ" n="5" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>; (Msb, K;) <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  <hi rend="ital">He sent to the woman her dowry;</hi> (K, TA;) or <hi rend="ital">conveyed it,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">caused it to be conveyed, to her;</hi> (Msb;) though consisting of dirhems or deenárs; because the dowry, with the Arabs, originally consisted of camels, which are driven. (TA.) And hence, <foreign lang="ar">مَاسُقْتَ إِلَيْهَا</foreign>, meaning <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">What didst thou give her as her dowry?</hi> occurring in a trad.; or, as some related it, <foreign lang="ar">مَا سُقْتَ مِنْهَا</foreign>, i. e. <hi rend="ital">What didst thou give for her,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">in exchange for her?</hi> (TA.) And <foreign lang="ar">ساق إِلَيْهِ الشَّىْءَ</foreign> <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  [<hi rend="ital">He made,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">caused, the thing to go, pass,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">be conveyed</hi> or <hi rend="ital">transmitted, to him; he sent to him the thing</hi>]. (M and K in art. <foreign lang="ar">اتى</foreign>.) And <foreign lang="ar">ساق إِلَيْهِ خَيْرًا</foreign> <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  [<hi rend="ital">He caused good,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">good fortune, to betide him</hi>]. (TA.) And <foreign lang="ar">ساق لِأَرْضِهِ أَتِيًّا</foreign> <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  [<hi rend="ital">He made a rivulet,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">a channel for water, to run to his land</hi>], (M in art. <foreign lang="ar">اتى</foreign>.)          <sense type="b" n="4">-b4-</sense>  [Hence likewise,] <foreign lang="ar">سَاقَتِ الرِّيحُ السَّحَابَ</foreign> <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  [<hi rend="ital">The wind drove along the clouds</hi>]. (S, * TA.)          <sense type="b" n="5">-b5-</sense>  [And <foreign lang="ar">ساق الحَدِيثَ</foreign>, inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">سِيَاقٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">سَوْقٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">مَسَاقٌ</foreign>, <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  <hi rend="ital">He carried on the narrative,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">discourse.</hi>] You say, <foreign lang="ar">فُلَانٌ يَسُوقُ الحَدِيثَ أَحْسَنَ سِيَاقٍ</foreign> <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  [<hi rend="ital">Such a one carries on the narrative,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">discourse, in the best manner of doing so</hi>]. (Mgh, TA.) And <foreign lang="ar">إِلَيْكَ يُسَاقُ الحَدِيثُ</foreign> <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  [<hi rend="ital">To thee</hi> as its object <hi rend="ital">the narrative,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">discourse, is carried on</hi>]. (TA.) And <foreign lang="ar">كَلَامٌ مَسَاقُهُ إِلَى كَذَا</foreign> <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  [<hi rend="ital">Speech whereof the</hi> 
                  <pb n="1471"/> 
                  <hi rend="ital">carrying-on is</hi> pointed <hi rend="ital">to such a thing</hi>]. (TA.) And <foreign lang="ar">جِئْتُكَ بِالحَدِيثِ عَلَى سَوْقِهِ</foreign> <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  [<hi rend="ital">I uttered to thee the narrative,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">discourse, after the proper manner of the carrying-on thereof</hi>]. (TA.) [In like manner also one says,] <foreign lang="ar">ساق الأُمُورَ أَحْسَنَ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">مَسَاقٍ</foreign> <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  [<hi rend="ital">He carried on,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">prosecuted, affairs,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">the affairs, in the best manner of doing so</hi>]. (A in art. <foreign lang="ar">حوذ</foreign>.)          <sense type="b" n="6">-b6-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">سَوْقُ المَعْلُومِ مَسَاقَ غَيْرِهِ</foreign> [from <foreign lang="ar">ساق الحَدِيثَ</foreign> expl. above] means <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">The asking respecting that which one knows in the manner of one's asking respecting that which he knows not:</hi> a mode of speech implying hyperbole: <hi rend="ital">as when one says,</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">أَوَجْهُكَ هٰذَا أَمْ بَدْرٌ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Is this thy face or a full moon?</hi>].                      <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">سَاقٌ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form> The <hi rend="ital">shank;</hi> i. e. the <hi rend="ital">part between the knee and the foot</hi> of a human being; (Msb;) or the <hi rend="ital">part between the ankle and the knee</hi> (K, TA) of a human being; (TA;) the <foreign lang="ar">ساق</foreign> of the human foot: (S, TA:) and [the <hi rend="ital">part properly corresponding thereto,</hi> i. e. the <hi rend="ital">thigh commonly so called,</hi> and also the <hi rend="ital">arm,</hi> of a beast;] the <hi rend="ital">part above the</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">وَظِيف</foreign> of the horse and mule and ass and camel, and the <hi rend="ital">part above the</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">كُرَاع</foreign> of the ox-kind and sheep or goat and antelope: (TA:) [it is also sometimes applied to the <hi rend="ital">shank commonly so called, of the hind leg,</hi> and, less properly, <hi rend="ital">of the fore leg,</hi> of a beast: and to the <hi rend="ital">bone of any of the parts above mentioned:</hi> and sometimes, by synecdoche, to the <hi rend="ital">hind leg,</hi> and, less properly, to the <hi rend="ital">fore leg</hi> also, of a beast: it generally corresponds to <foreign lang="ar">ذِرَاعٌ</foreign>: of a bird, it is the <hi rend="ital">thigh commonly so called:</hi> and sometimes the <hi rend="ital">shank commonly so called:</hi> and, by synecdoche, the <hi rend="ital">leg:</hi>] it is of the fem. gender: (Msb, TA:) and for this reason, (TA,) the dim. is   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n21288-1" target="سُوَيْقَةٌ" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n21297"/></foreign>: (Msb, TA:) the pl. [of mult.] is <foreign lang="ar">سُوقٌ</foreign> (S, Mgh, O, Msb, K) and <foreign lang="ar">سِيقَانٌ</foreign> and [of pauc.] <foreign lang="ar">أَسْؤُقٌ</foreign>, (S, O, K,) the <foreign lang="ar">و</foreign> in this last being with <foreign lang="ar">ء</foreign> in order that it may bear the dammeh. (O, K.) A poet says, <quote>
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">لِلْفَتَى عَقْلٌ يَعِيشُ بِهِ</foreign>
                     </L> 
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">حَيْثُ تَهْدِى سَاقَهُ قَدَمُهْ</foreign>
                     </L> 
                  </quote> meaning <hi rend="ital">The young man has intelligence whereby he lives when his foot directs aright his shank.</hi> (IAar, TA.) And one says of a man when difficulty, or calamity, befalls him, <foreign lang="ar">كَشَفَ عَنْ سَاقِهِ</foreign> [lit. <hi rend="ital">He uncovered his shank;</hi> meaning <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">he prepared himself for difficulty</hi>]: so says IAmb: and hence, he says, (TA, [in which a similar explanation is cited from ISd also,]) they mention the <foreign lang="ar">ساق</foreign> when they mean to express the difficulty of a case or an event, and to tell of the terror occasioned thereby. (K, TA.) Thus, the saying <foreign lang="ar">يَوْمَ يُكْشَفُ عَنْ سَاقٍ</foreign>, (S, K, TA,) in the Kur [lxviii. 42], (S, TA,) [lit. <hi rend="ital">On a day when a shank shall be uncovered,</hi>] means <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">on a day when difficulty,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">calamity, shall be disclosed.</hi> (I'Ab, Mujáhid, S, K, TA.) It is like the saying, <foreign lang="ar">قَامَتِ الحَرْبُ عَلَى سَاقٍ</foreign>, (S, TA,) which means <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">The war,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">battle, became vehement,</hi> (Msb in this art. and in art. <foreign lang="ar">حرب</foreign>,) <hi rend="ital">so that safety from destruction was difficult of attainment:</hi> (Id. in art. <foreign lang="ar">حرب</foreign>:) and <foreign lang="ar">كَشَفَتِ الحَرْبُ عَنْ سَاقٍ</foreign>, [as also <foreign lang="ar">شَمَّرَتْ عَنْ سَاقِهَا</foreign>,] i. e. <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">The war,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">battle, became vehement.</hi> (Jel in lxviii. 42.) And in like manner, <foreign lang="ar">وَٱلْتَفَّتِ ٱلسَّاقُ بِالسَّاقِ</foreign>, (K, TA,) in the Kur [lxxv. 29], (TA,) means <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">And the affliction of the present state of existence shall be combined with that of the final state:</hi> (K, TA:) or it means <hi rend="ital">when the</hi> [one] <hi rend="ital">leg shall be inwrapped with the</hi> other <hi rend="ital">leg by means of the grave-clothes.</hi> (TA.)                   <foreign lang="ar">تَنْضُب</foreign>, <hi rend="ital">he will not loose the stem</hi> thereof <hi rend="ital">unless grasping a stem</hi>]: he meant that no plea of his came to nought but he clung to another; likening him to the chameleon, which places itself facing the sun, and ascends half-way up the tree, or shrub, then climbs to the branches when the sun becomes hot, then climbs to a higher branch, and will not loose the former until it grasps the other.                      <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">سُوقٌ</orth>
